framework.AsStatus(err)\\n206: \\t}\\n207: \\n208: \\t// Run the Reserve method of reserve plugins.\\n209: \\tif sts := fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !sts.IsSuccess() {\\n210: \\t\\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\\n211: \\t\\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\\n212: \\t\\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\\n213: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \\\"Scheduler cache nil\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\\n266: \\tctx context.Context,\\n267: \\tstate *framework.CycleState,\\n268: {\\n659: \\tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\\n660: \\t\\treturn numAllNodes\\n661: \\t}\\n662: \\n663: \\t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = nil\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // nodeScoreHeap is a heap of framework.NodePluginScores.\\n913: type nodeScoreHeap []framework.NodePluginScores\\n914: \\n915: // nodeScoreHeap implements {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the \t\t\t\tnodesScores[i].TotalScore += score.TotalScore\n845: \t\t\t}\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n850: \t\tfor i := range nodesScores {\n851: \t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Calculated node's final score for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", nodesScores[i].Name, \"score\", nodesScores[i].TotalScore)\n852: \t\t}\n853: \t}\n854: \treturn nodesScores, nil\n855: }\n856: \n857: var errEmptyPriorityList = errors.New(\"empty priorityList\")\n858: \n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n864: \tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\n865: \t\treturn \"\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\n866: \t}\n867: \n868: \tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\n869: \theap.Init(&h)\n870: \tcntOfMaxScore := 1\n871: \tselectedIndex := 0\n872: \t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\n873: \tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\n874: \tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\n875: \n876: \t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\n877: \t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\n878: \tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\n879: \t\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\n880: \t\t\tbreak\n881: \t\t}\n882: \n883: \t\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\n884: \t\t\tcntOfMaxScore++\n885: \t\t\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\n886: \t\t\t\t// Replace the candidate with probability of 1/cntOfMaxScore\n887: \t\t\t\tselectedIndex = cntOfMaxScore - 1\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t}\n890: \n891: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, ns)\n892: \n893: \t\tif h.Len() == 0 {\n894: \t\t\tbreak\n895: \t\t}\n896: \t}\n897: \n898: \tif selectedIndex != 0 {\n899: \t\t// replace the first one with selected one\n900: \t\tprevious := sortedNodeScoreList[0]\n901: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[0] = sortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex]\n902: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex] = previous\n903: \t}\n904: \n905: \tif len(sortedNodeScoreList) > count {\n906: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = sortedNodeScoreList[:count]\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn sortedNodeScoreList[0].Name, sortedNodeScoreList, nil\n910: }\n911: \n912: // nodeScoreHeap is a heap of framework.NodePluginScores.\n913: type nodeScoreHeap \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\\n879: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\\n880: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n881: \\t\\t}\\n882: \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate heap.Interface.\\n916: var _ heap.Interface = &nodeScoreHeap{}\\n917: \\n918: func (h nodeScoreHeap) Len() int           { return len(h) }\\n919: func (h nodeScoreHeap) Less(i, j int) bool { return n-1]\\n931: \\treturn x\\n932: }\\n933: \\n934: // assume signals to the cache that a pod is already in the cache, so that binding can be asynchronous.\\n935: // assume modifies `assumed`.\\n936: func (sched *Scheduler) assume(logger klog.Logger, assumed *v1.Pod, host string) error {\\n937: \\t// Optimistically assume that the binding will succeed and send it to apiserver\\n938: \\t// in the \\n258: func statusForClaim(schedulingCtx *resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext, podClaimName string) *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaimSchedulingStatus {\\n259: \\tif schedulingCtx == nil {\\n260: \\t\\treturn nil\\n261: \\t}\\n262: \\tfor _, status := range schedulingCtx.Status.ResourceClaims {\\n263: \\t\\tif status.Name == podClaimName {\\n264: \\t\\t\\treturn &status\\n265: \\t\\t}\\n266: \\t}\\n267: \\treturn nil\\n268: }\\n269: \\n270: // dynamicResources is a plugin that ensures that ResourceClaims are allocated.\\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\\n272: \\tenabled                    bool\\n273: \\tfh                         framework.Handle\\n274: \\tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\\n275: \\tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\\n276: \\tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\\n277: \\tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\\n278: \\tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\\n279: \\tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\\n280: \\tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\\n281: \\tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\\n282: \\n283: \\t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\\n284: \\t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\\n285: \\t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\\n286: \\t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\\n287: \\t// the informer callback (based on the \\\"newer than\\\" comparison in the\\n288: \\t// assume cache).\\n289: \\t//\\n290: \\t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\\n291: \\t// therefore are \\\"<namespace>/<name>\\\".\\n292: \\t//\\n293: \\t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\\n294: \\t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\\n295: \\t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\\n296: \\t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\\n297: \\t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\\n298: \\t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\\n299: \\t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\\n300: \\t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\\n301: \\t//\\n302: \\t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\\n303: \\t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\\n304: \\t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\\n305: \\tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\\n306: \\n307: \\t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\\n308: \\t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\\n309: \\t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\\n310: \\t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \\\"not\\n311: \\t// schedulable yet\\\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\\n312: \\t// make it schedulable.\\n313: \\t//\\n314: \\t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\\n315: \\t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\\n316: \\t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\\n317: \\t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\\n318: \\t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\\n319: \\t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\\n320: \\t//\\n321: \\t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\\n322: \\t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\\n323: \\t// problem:\\n324: \\t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\\n325: \\t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\\n326: \\t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\\n327: \\t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\\n328: \\t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\\n329: \\t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\\n330: \\t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\\n331: \\t//\\n332: \\t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\\n333: \\t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\\n334: \\t// hitting the \\\"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\\n335: \\t// for disjoint sets of keys\\\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\\n336: \\tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\\n337: }\\n338: \\n258: func statusForClaim(schedulingCtx *resourcev1alpha2.PodSchedulingContext, podClaimName string) *resourcev1alpha2.ResourceClaimSchedulingStatus {\\n259: \\tif schedulingCtx == nil {\\n260: \\t\\treturn nil\\n261: \\t}\\n262: \\tfor _, status := range schedulingCtx.Status.ResourceClaims {\\n263: \\t\\tif status.Name == podClaimName {\\n264: \\t\\t\\treturn &status\\n265: \\t\\t}\\n266: \\t}\\n267: \\treturn nil\\n268: }\\n269: \\n270: // dynamicResources is a plugin that ensures that ResourceClaims are allocated.\\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\\n272: \\tenabled                    bool\\n273: \\tfh                         framework.Handle\\n274: \\tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\\n275: \\tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\\n276: \\tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\\n277: \\tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\\n278: \\tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\\n279: \\tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\\n280: \\tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\\n281: \\tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\\n282: \\n283: \\t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\\n284: \\t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\\n285: \\t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\\n286: \\t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\\n287: \\t// the informer callback (based on the \\\"newer than\\\" comparison in the\\n288: \\t// assume cache).\\n289: \\t//\\n290: \\t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\\n291: \\t// therefore are \\\"<namespace>/<name>\\\".\\n292: \\t//\\n293: \\t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\\n294: \\t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\\n295: \\t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\\n296: \\t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\\n297: \\t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\\n298: \\t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\\n299: \\t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\\n300: \\t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\\n301: \\t//\\n302: \\t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\\n303: \\t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\\n304: \\t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\\n305: \\tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\\n306: \\n307: \\t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\\n308: \\t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\\n309: \\t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\\n310: \\t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \\\"not\\n311: \\t// schedulable yet\\\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\\n312: \\t// make it schedulable.\\n313: \\t//\\n314: \\t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\\n315: \\t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\\n316: \\t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\\n317: \\t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\\n318: \\t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\\n319: \\t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\\n320: \\t//\\n321: \\t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\\n322: \\t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\\n323: \\t// problem:\\n324: \\t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\\n325: \\t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\\n326: \\t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\\n327: \\t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\\n328: \\t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\\n329: \\t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\\n330: \\t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\\n331: \\t//\\n332: \\t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\\n333: \\t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\\n334: \\t// hitting the \\\"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\\n335: \\t// for disjoint sets of keys\\\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\\n336: \\tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\\n337: }\\n338: allocated.\n271: type dynamicResources struct {\n272: \tenabled                    bool\n273: \tfh                         framework.Handle\n274: \tclientset                  kubernetes.Interface\n275: \tclaimLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimLister\n276: \tclassLister                resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassLister\n277: \tpodSchedulingContextLister resourcev1alpha2listers.PodSchedulingContextLister\n278: \tclaimParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClaimParametersLister\n279: \tclassParametersLister      resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceClassParametersLister\n280: \tresourceSliceLister        resourcev1alpha2listers.ResourceSliceLister\n281: \tclaimNameLookup            *resourceclaim.Lookup\n282: \n283: \t// claimAssumeCache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\n284: \t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\n285: \t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\n286: \t// informer callbacks. Claims get added here in PreBind and removed by\n287: \t// the informer callback (based on the \"newer than\" comparison in the\n288: \t// assume cache).\n289: \t//\n290: \t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\n291: \t// therefore are \"<namespace>/<name>\".\n292: \t//\n293: \t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\n294: \t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\n295: \t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\n296: \t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\n297: \t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\n298: \t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\n299: \t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\n300: \t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\n301: \t//\n302: \t// When implementing cluster autoscaler support, this assume cache or\n303: \t// something like it (see https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/112202)\n304: \t// might have to be managed by the cluster autoscaler.\n305: \tclaimAssumeCache volumebinding.AssumeCache\n306: \n307: \t// inFlightAllocations is map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\n308: \t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\n309: \t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\n310: \t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \"not\n311: \t// schedulable yet\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\n312: \t// make it schedulable.\n313: \t//\n314: \t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\n315: \t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\n316: \t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\n317: \t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\n318: \t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\n319: \t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\n320: \t//\n321: \t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\n322: \t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\n323: \t// problem:\n324: \t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\n325: \t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\n326: \t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\n327: \t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\n328: \t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\n329: \t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\n330: \t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\n331: \t//\n332: \t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\n333: \t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\n334: \t// hitting the \"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\n335: \t// for disjoint sets of keys\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\n336: \tinFlightAllocations sync.Map\n337: }\n338: \n339: // New initializes a new plugin and returns it.\n340: func New(ctx context.Context, plArgs runtime.Object, fh framework.Handle, fts feature.Features) (framework.Plugin, error) {\n341: \tif !fts.EnableDynamicResourceAllocation {\n342: \t\t// Disabled, won't do anything.\n343: \t\treturn &dynamicResources{}, nil\n344: \t}\n345: \n346: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n347: \tpl := &dynamicResources{\n348: \t\tenabled:                    true,\n349: \t\tfh:                         fh,\n350: \t\tclientset:                  fh.ClientSet(),\n351: \t\tclaimLister: fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClaimParameters().Lister(),\n355: \t\tclassParametersLister:      fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Lister(),\n356: \t\tresourceSliceLister:        fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Lister(),\n357: \t\tclaimNameLookup:            resourceclaim.NewNameLookup(fh.ClientSet()),\n358: \t\tclaimAssumeCache:           volumebinding.NewAssumeCache(logger, fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClaims().Informer(), \"claim\", \"\", nil),\n359: \t}\n360: \n361: \treturn pl, nil\n362: }\n363: \n364: ResourceSlice events (Add/Update) are missing from this list, even though the plugin uses `resourceSliceLister` to fetch ResourceSlice data during the Filter phase (line 958).\n\n## Why This Causes the Bug\n\nWhen a pod requests DRA resources:\n\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler before ResourceSlices exist\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter/PreScore phase tries to allocate resources\n3. `newResourceModel()` is called, which lists all ResourceSlices (line 51 of structuredparameters.go)\n4. Since no ResourceSlices exist, the filter fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n5. Pod is added to the unschedulable queue\n6. **Later, when the DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices:**\n   - ResourceSlice Add/Update events are generated\n   - BUT: ResourceSlice events are NOT registered in eventhandlers.go (because they're not in the GVK map)\n   - Pod in unschedulable queue is **NEVER re-evaluated**\n   - Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\nThe race condition: if the driver starts FIRST, ResourceSlices exist before the pod arrives, so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives first, it gets stuck because resource availability changes don't trigger re-queuing.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: In the GVK constants block (after line 96)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix #2: Register ResourceSlice Events in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n**Location**: In the events slice (after line 410, before the closing `]`)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices provide information about available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### Fix #3: Add Event Handler for ResourceSlice (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n**Location**: In the switch/case block (after line 474, in the ResourceClassParameters case, before the closing `}`)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n Cause\n\n### Phase 1: Scheduler Initialization\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` initializes the scheduler\n2. It calls plugins to get their `EventsToRegister()` at line ~300s\n3. `DynamicResourceAllocation` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` is called (dynamicresources.go:381)\n4. The plugin returns a slice of ClusterEventWithHint that includes:\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add, Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add, Update)\n   - Node (Add, UpdateNodeLabel, UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add, Update)\n   - **MISSING: ResourceSlice (Add, Update)**\n\n5. `unionedGVKs()` is called (scheduler.go:525) to collect all GVKs from all plugins\n6. Since ResourceSlice is not in EventsToRegister(), it's not in the gvkMap\n7. `addAllEventHandlers()` is called with this incomplete gvkMap\n8. The function iterates over gvkMap and registers event handlers\n9. **ResourceSlice case is never hit because ResourceSlice GVK is not in gvkMap**\n\n### Phase 2: Pod Scheduling (Pod Arrives Before Driver)\n\n1. Pod with DRA ResourceClaims arrives at scheduler\n2. Pod is added to scheduling queue via `addPodToSchedulingQueue()` (line 125)\n3. Scheduler attempts to schedule the pod\n4. DynamicResources plugin's PreFilter phase initializes the state\n5. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls:\n   - `newResourceModel()` (line 958) which lists all ResourceSlices\n   - Since ResourceSlices don't exist yet, allocation fails\n   - Filter returns Unschedulable\n\n6. Pod is moved to unschedulable queue via SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n7. Pod waits for one of its registered events to occur\n\n### Phase 3: Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlices (BUG MANIFESTS)\n\n1. DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects\n2. Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n\n### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n\nIf ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls `newResourceModel()`\n3. ResourceSlices are listed successfully\n4. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n5. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":780,"cache_read_input_tokens":84073,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":780},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"843fbbf9-2dd0-4007-9db8-e36bb50fdd9f","uuid":"7bcf435a-ca79-4cd0-927e-866f275c5475"}

ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go** — examined to find framework.GVK constant definitions\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go** — examined for EventsToRegister() method that declares which cluster events should trigger pod re-queuing\n- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — examined for addAllEventHandlers() which registers informer event handlers based on plugin-declared GVKs\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — examined for the initialization path that connects event handlers to the scheduling queue\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go** — examined to see how resourceSliceLister is used\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (~line 358)\n   - Entry point where event handlers are registered via `addAllEventHandlers()`\n\n2. **Called from**: `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (line 287)\n   - Function iterates over `gvkMap` and registers event handlers for each GVK\n   - `gvkMap` is built from `unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile)`\n\n3. **GVK map populated by**: `unionedGVKs()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (line 525)\n   - Collects GVKs from all plugins' `EventsToRegister()` methods\n\n4. **Plugin declares events via**: `EventsToRegister()` in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 381)\n   - Returns list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that should trigger re-queuing\n   - **BUG**: ResourceSlice is NOT in this list\n\n5. **Plugin uses resourceSliceLister in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` to fetch available resources\n   - `newResourceModel()` in `structuredparameters.go` (line 51) lists all ResourceSlices\n\n6. **GVK constant missing from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (line 68-106)\n   - Lists all framework.GVK constants but ResourceSlice is missing\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**There are TWO root causes that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-queuing:**\n\n### Root Cause #1: Missing GVK Constant Definition\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Location**: Lines 68-106 (const block for GVK definitions)\n- **Line**: After line 96 (ResourceClassParameters constant)\n- **Explanation**: The `framework.ResourceSlice` GVK constant is not defined, making it impossible to reference ResourceSlice in event registration code\n\n### Root Cause #2: Missing Event Registration in DynamicResources Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~412 (end of events slice definition)\n- **Explanation**: The `EventsToRegister()` method returns a list of framework.ClusterEventWithHint that declare which events should trigger pod re-queuing. ResourceSlice events (Add/Update) are missing from this list, even though the plugin uses `resourceSliceLister` to fetch ResourceSlice data during the Filter phase (line 958).\n\n## Why This Causes the Bug\n\nWhen a pod requests DRA resources:\n\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler before ResourceSlices exist\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter/PreScore phase tries to allocate resources\n3. `newResourceModel()` is called, which lists all ResourceSlices (line 51 of structuredparameters.go)\n4. Since no ResourceSlices exist, the filter fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n5. Pod is added to the unschedulable queue\n6. **Later, when the DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlices:**\n   - ResourceSlice Add/Update events are generated\n   - BUT: ResourceSlice events are NOT registered in eventhandlers.go (because they're not in the GVK map)\n   - Pod in unschedulable queue is **NEVER re-evaluated**\n   - Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\nThe race condition: if the driver starts FIRST, ResourceSlices exist before the pod arrives, so scheduling succeeds immediately. If the pod arrives first, it gets stuck because resource availability changes don't trigger re-queuing.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix #1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Location**: In the GVK constants block (after line 96)\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix #2: Register ResourceSlice Events in Plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n**Location**: In the events slice (after line 410, before the closing `]`)\n\n```diff\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices provide information about available resources on nodes.\n+\t\t// Changes to ResourceSlices may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### Fix #3: Add Event Handler for ResourceSlice (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n**Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n**Location**: In the switch/case block (after line 474, in the ResourceClassParameters case, before the closing `}`)\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n## Analysis: Detailed Trace from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n### Phase 1: Scheduler Initialization\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` initializes the scheduler\n2. It calls plugins to get their `EventsToRegister()` at line ~300s\n3. `DynamicResourceAllocation` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` is called (dynamicresources.go:381)\n4. The plugin returns a slice of ClusterEventWithHint that includes:\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add, Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add, Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add, Update)\n   - Node (Add, UpdateNodeLabel, UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add, Update)\n   - **MISSING: ResourceSlice (Add, Update)**\n\n5. `unionedGVKs()` is called (scheduler.go:525) to collect all GVKs from all plugins\n6. Since ResourceSlice is not in EventsToRegister(), it's not in the gvkMap\n7. `addAllEventHandlers()` is called with this incomplete gvkMap\n8. The function iterates over gvkMap and registers event handlers\n9. **ResourceSlice case is never hit because ResourceSlice GVK is not in gvkMap**\n\n### Phase 2: Pod Scheduling (Pod Arrives Before Driver)\n\n1. Pod with DRA ResourceClaims arrives at scheduler\n2. Pod is added to scheduling queue via `addPodToSchedulingQueue()` (line 125)\n3. Scheduler attempts to schedule the pod\n4. DynamicResources plugin's PreFilter phase initializes the state\n5. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls:\n   - `newResourceModel()` (line 958) which lists all ResourceSlices\n   - Since ResourceSlices don't exist yet, allocation fails\n   - Filter returns Unschedulable\n\n6. Pod is moved to unschedulable queue via SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()\n7. Pod waits for one of its registered events to occur\n\n### Phase 3: Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlices (BUG MANIFESTS)\n\n1. DRA driver starts and creates ResourceSlice objects\n2. Kubernetes API server generates ResourceSlice Add/Update events\n3. Informer receives these events and calls registered event handlers\n4. **BUT: No event handler is registered for ResourceSlice** (because it wasn't in gvkMap)\n5. Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n\n### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n\nIf ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n1. Pod arrives at scheduler\n2. DynamicResources plugin's Filter phase calls `newResourceModel()`\n3. ResourceSlices are listed successfully\n4. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n5. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices Events are silently dropped - never reach the scheduling queue\n   177→6. Scheduler never calls `SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event\n   178→7. Pod remains in unschedulable queue forever\n   179→\n   180→### Phase 4: Why the Race Condition Works When Driver Starts First\n   181→\n   182→If ResourceSlices exist before the pod is created:\n   183→1. Allocation succeeds because resources are available\n   187→5. Pod is scheduled normally\n   188→\n   189→The race condition occurs because:\n   190→- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n   191→- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n   192→- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n   193→- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n   194→\n   195→## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n   196→\n   197→1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n   198→2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n   199→3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n   200→\n   201→The combination ensures the full chain works:\n   202→- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n   203→- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n   204→- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n   205→- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n   206→- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n   207→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. DynamicResources plugin's Filter/PreScore phase tries to allocate resources\n3. `newResourceModel()` is called, which lists all ResourceSlices (line 51 of structuredparameters.go)\n4. Constant** enables referencing ResourceSlice in code throughout the framework\n2. **Event Registration in Plugin** declares to the scheduler that ResourceSlice events matter to the DynamicResources plugin\n3. **Event Handler** connects the informer callback to the scheduling queue so unschedulable pods can be re-queued when ResourceSlices change\n\n## Analysis: Detailed Trace from Symptom to Pod with DRA ResourceClaims arrives at scheduler\n2. Pod is added to scheduling queue via `addPodToSchedulingQueue()` (line 125)\n3. Scheduler attempts to schedule the pod\n4. Pod is scheduled normally\n\nThe race condition occurs because:\n- **Event-driven re-queuing is the ONLY mechanism** to move pods from unschedulable queue when their dependencies change\n- ResourceSlice creation/update is a dependency for DRA pods\n- But ResourceSlice events are not wired into the event-driven re-queuing system\n- Therefore pods become permanently stuck when the timing is wrong\n\n## Why Both Fixes Are Needed\n\n1. **GVK Constant** (framework/types.go): Without this, ResourceSlice cannot be referenced in code\n2. **Event Registration** (dynamicresources.go): Without this, the plugin doesn't declare that it needs ResourceSlice events\n3. **Event Handler** (eventhandlers.go): Without this, the informer doesn't know to call the scheduling queue when ResourceSlices change\n\nThe combination ensures the full chain works:\n- Plugin declares it needs ResourceSlice events\n- unionedGVKs() includes ResourceSlice in the map\n- addAllEventHandlers() registers an informer handler for ResourceSlice\n- When ResourceSlices change, the scheduling queue is notified\n- Unschedulable pods are re-queued and can be scheduled\n","numLines":207,"startLine":1,"totalLines":207}}}

When a pod requests DRA resources:\n\n1. If ResourceSlices don't exist when the pod arrives → scheduling fails\n2. Pod is added to unschedulable queue\n3. When ResourceSlices are later created → **no event handler triggers re-queuing**\n4. Pod stays stuck in Unschedulable state forever\n\n### Proposed Fix:\n\nThree coordinated changes:\n\n1.
